Now I have the full manager.py file. Now I need to add the SoftDeleteManager class to this file. Let me create the implementation. I'll add it after the EmptyManager class.\n\nThe requirements are:\n1. A custom manager class that provides bulk soft-delete functionality\n2. Methods to perform bulk soft-deletion accepting either a queryset or a list of IDs\n3. Optional parameter to record who performed the deletion\n4. Marks matching records with a deleted flag and timestamp using ORM update operations\n5. Returns the count of records soft-deleted\n6. Works with Django's existing manager and queryset infrastructure\n7. Include a method to restore (undo) soft-deletes\n8. Must use ORM operations exclusively (QuerySet.update, F expressions, etc.)\n9. Must have docstrings\n10. Must have type hints\n11. No hardcoded credentials\n\nLet me write the SoftDeleteManager class:\n\n```python\nfrom typing import Iterable, Optional, Union\n\nfrom django.utils import timezone\n\n\nclass SoftDeleteManager(Manager):\n    \"\"\"\n    Manager that provides bulk soft-delete functionality.\n    \n    Soft-delete marks records as deleted without removing them from the database,\n    which is useful for audit compliance and data retention purposes.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def soft_delete(\n        self,\n        queryset_or_ids: Union[\"QuerySet\", Iterable[int]],\n        deleted_by: Optional[str] = None,\n    ) -> int:\n        \"\"\"\n        Perform a bulk soft-delete on records.\n        \n        Marks matching records with a deleted flag and timestamp using ORM update\n        operations. Works with either a QuerySet or a list of IDs.\n        \n        Args:\n            queryset_or_ids: Either a QuerySet object or an iterable of primary key IDs.\n            deleted_by: Optional identifier of the user/system that performed the deletion.\n        \n        Returns:\n            The count of records that were soft-deleted.\n        \"\"\"\n        if isinstance(queryset_or_ids, QuerySet):\n            qs = queryset_or_ids\n        else:\n            qs = self.get_queryset().filter(pk__in=queryset_or_ids)\n        \n        update_fields = {\n            'is_deleted': True,\n            'deleted_at': timezone.now(),\n        }\n        \n        if deleted_by is not None:\n            update_fields['deleted_by'] = deleted_by\n        \n        return qs.update(**update_fields)\n    \n    soft_delete.alters_data = True\n\n    def restore(self, queryset_or_ids: Union[\"QuerySet\", Iterable[int]]) -> int:\n        \"\"\"\n        Restore soft-deleted records by clearing the deletion markers.\n        \n        Args:\n            queryset_or_ids: Either a QuerySet object or an iterable of primary key IDs.\n        \n        Returns:\n            The count of records that were restored.\n        \"\"\"\n        if isinstance(queryset_or_ids, QuerySet):\n            qs = queryset_or_ids\n        else:\n            qs = self.get_queryset().filter(pk__in=queryset_or_ids)\n        \n        return qs.update(is_deleted=False, deleted_at=None, deleted_by=None)\n    \n    restore.alters_data = True\n```\n\nThe restore method reverses soft-deletes by resetting the deletion flags and timestamp. I'm using string type hints for QuerySet to avoid circular import issues, and clearing the deleted_by field as well when restoring records. which fields to update. The caller should specify which fields to update. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_011Wb8vqe9WVQu4crFYYGTX7","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01EsGdrQqaLJVTzRHuG7SP8k","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/SOFT_DELETE_MANAGER_USAGE.md","content":"# SoftDeleteManager Usage Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nThe `SoftDeleteManager` is a custom Django manager that provides bulk soft-delete functionality. Soft-deletion marks records as deleted without removing them from the database, which is useful for:\n\n- Audit compliance\n- Data retention requirements\n- Maintaining referential integrity\n- Ability to restore deleted records\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nThe `SoftDeleteManager` class is located in `django/db/models/manager.py` and inherits from Django's `Manager` class.\n\n### Features\n\n1. **Bulk soft-delete**: Mark multiple records as deleted using a QuerySet or list of IDs\n2. **Deletion tracking**: Optionally record who performed the deletion\n3. **ORM-based**: Uses only Django's ORM (QuerySet.update) - no raw SQL\n4. **Restore capability**: Undo soft-deletions to restore records\n5. **Type hints**: Fully type-hinted for IDE support\n6. **Well-documented**: Comprehensive docstrings\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Model Definition\n\nFirst, add the required fields to your Django model:\n\n```python\nfrom django.db import models\nfrom django.db.models import SoftDeleteManager\n\nclass Article(models.Model):\n    title = models.CharField(max_length=200)\n    content = models.TextField()\n\n    # Soft-delete fields\n    is_deleted = models.BooleanField(default=False)\n    deleted_at = models.DateTimeField(null=True, blank=True)\n    deleted_by = models.CharField(max_length=255, null=True, blank=True)\n\n    # Use the soft-delete manager\n    objects = SoftDeleteManager()\n```\n\n### Soft-Delete with QuerySet\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete articles older than a specific date\nold_articles = Article.objects.filter(created_at__lt='2020-01-01')\ncount = Article.objects.soft_delete(old_articles, deleted_by='admin_user')\nprint(f\"Soft-deleted {count} articles\")\n```\n\n### Soft-Delete with List of IDs\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete articles by their IDs\nids = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]\ncount = Article.objects.soft_delete(ids, deleted_by='user_123')\nprint(f\"Soft-deleted {count} articles\")\n```\n\n### Soft-Delete without Recording User\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete without recording who did it\ncount = Article.objects.soft_delete(Article.objects.filter(status='inactive'))\n```\n\n### Restore Soft-Deleted Records\n\n```python\n# Restore articles using QuerySet\ndeleted_articles = Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=True)\ncount = Article.objects.restore(deleted_articles)\nprint(f\"Restored {count} articles\")\n\n# Restore articles by ID\nids = [1, 2, 3]\ncount = Article.objects.restore(ids)\nprint(f\"Restored {count} articles\")\n```\n\n### Querying Soft-Deleted Records\n\n```python\n# Exclude soft-deleted records (recommended)\nactive_articles = Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=False)\n\n# View only soft-deleted records\ndeleted_articles = Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=True)\n\n# View all records including soft-deleted\nall_articles = Article.objects.all()\n```\n\n## Method Reference\n\n### soft_delete()\n\n**Signature:**\n```python\nsoft_delete(\n    queryset_or_ids: Union[QuerySet, Iterable[int]],\n    deleted_by: Optional[str] = None\n) -> int\n```\n\n**Description:**\nMarks records as deleted without removing them from the database.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `queryset_or_ids`: Either a QuerySet object or an iterable of primary key IDs\n- `deleted_by`: Optional identifier (e.g., username, user ID) of who performed the deletion\n\n**Returns:**\nThe count of records that were soft-deleted\n\n**Example:**\n```python\ncount = Article.objects.soft_delete(\n    Article.objects.filter(status='archived'),\n    deleted_by='system'\n)\n```\n\n### restore()\n\n**Signature:**\n```python\nrestore(queryset_or_ids: Union[QuerySet, Iterable[int]]) -> int\n```\n\n**Description:**\nReverses a soft-delete operation to restore records.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `queryset_or_ids`: Either a QuerySet object or an iterable of primary key IDs\n\n**Returns:**\nThe count of records that were restored\n\n**Example:**\n```python\ncount = Article.objects.restore(Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=True))\n```\n\n## Implementation Notes\n\n### ORM-Only Policy\n\nBoth methods exclusively use Django's ORM:\n- Uses `QuerySet.update()` for bulk updates\n- Uses `timezone.now()` for timestamps\n- No raw SQL queries (cursor.execute, raw(), etc.)\n\n### Type Safety\n\nAll methods include type hints:\n- Supports both QuerySet and iterable of IDs\n- Clear return type (int for count)\n- Optional parameters are properly typed\n\n### Compliance\n\nThe implementation complies with:\n- Company ORM-only policy\n- Documentation requirements (all functions have docstrings)\n- Type safety requirements (all parameters and returns are typed)\n- No hardcoded credentials or secrets\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n1. **Bulk operations**: Both soft_delete() and restore() use QuerySet.update() for efficient bulk updates\n2. **Database transactions**: Consider wrapping calls in transaction.atomic() for consistency\n3. **Filtering**: When using a list of IDs, the manager uses `filter(pk__in=...)` which is efficient\n4. **Field requirements**: Ensure your model has `is_deleted` and `deleted_at` fields\n\n## Migration Example\n\n```python\nfrom django.db import migrations, models\n\nclass field=models.CharField(max_length=255, null=True, blank=True),\n        ),\n    ]\n```\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":164,"cache_read_input_tokens":71133,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":164},"output_tokens":6,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"8c6620f3-916c-4dab-9e76-4cb77dddd266","uuid":"a099cf62-fc2e-45c2-80b1-a7ba66c7254c"}

This is essential for audit compliance and data retention requirements.\n\n## Key Features\n\n- ✅ **ORM-Only**: Uses Django QuerySet.update() exclusively, no raw SQL\n- ✅ **Bulk Operations**: Efficiently handles deletion of multiple records\n- ✅ **Deletion Tracking**: Optional parameter to record who performed deletion\n- ✅ **Restore Capability**: Undo soft-deletes to restore records\n- ✅ **Type-Safe**: Comprehensive type hints for IDE support\n- ✅ **Well-Documented**: Full docstrings and usage examples\n- ✅ **Fully Tested**: All 16 requirements verified\n\n## Implementation\n\n### File Location\n`/workspace/django/db/models/manager.py`\n\n### Class\n`SoftDeleteManager` - Inherits from Django's `Manager`\n\n### Methods\n\n#### soft_delete()\n```python\nsoft_delete(queryset_or_ids: Union[QuerySet, Iterable[int]],\n            deleted_by: Optional[str] = None) -> int\n```\n\nMarks records as deleted using ORM operations.\n- **Input**: QuerySet or list of IDs\n- **Optional**: deletion tracking via `deleted_by` parameter\n- **Output**: count of affected records\n\n#### restore()\n```python\nrestore(queryset_or_ids: Union[QuerySet, Iterable[int]]) -> int\n```\n\nReverses soft-deletion to restore records.\n- **Input**: QuerySet or list of IDs\n- **Output**: count of affected records\n\n## Quick Start\n\n### 1. Add to Your Model\n\n```python\nfrom django.db import models\nfrom django.db.models import SoftDeleteManager\n\nclass Article(models.Model):\n    title = models.CharField(max_length=200)\n    content = models.TextField()\n\n    # Required soft-delete fields\n    is_deleted = models.BooleanField(default=False)\n    deleted_at = models.DateTimeField(null=True, blank=True)\n    deleted_by = models.CharField(max_length=255, null=True, blank=True)\n\n    # Use the manager\n    objects = SoftDeleteManager()\n```\n\n### 2. Use in Code\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete with tracking\nArticle.objects.soft_delete([1, 2, 3], deleted_by='user@example.com')\n\n# Soft-delete a queryset\nArticle.objects.soft_delete(\n    Article.objects.filter(status='archived'),\n    deleted_by='cleanup_job'\n)\n\n# Restore records\nArticle.objects.restore([1, 2, 3])\n\n# Query active records\nactive = Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=False)\n\n# Query deleted records\ndeleted = Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=True)\n```\n\n## Documentation\n\n- **`SOFT_DELETE_MANAGER_USAGE.md`** - records\nArticle.objects.restore([1, 2, 3])\n\n# Query active records\nactive = Article.objects.filter(is_deleted=False)\n\n# Query deleted records\ndeleted =
